<div id="storyImage">
<h1>Napoleon Dynamite</h1>
<img alt="Scene from 'Napoleon Dynamite'" class="multimedia1" src="/web/20141229133904im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/2004/ep20/napolean01.jpg"/>
<p class="description">Living in Preston, Idaho, with a red 'fro, wearing moon boots, doing 'sweet' bike jumps and illegal government ninja moves, Napoleon Dynamite is a new kind of high school hero.</p>
<p class="score" style="border:0;"> Margaret: <img alt="three-and-a-half stars" class="rating" src="/web/20141229133904im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/bthree-and-a-half.gif"/> David: <img alt="four stars" class="rating" src="/web/20141229133904im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/bfour.gif"/> </p>
</div>
<h3>Napoleon Dynamite</h3>
<p><em>Review by David Stratton</em></p>
<p>‘Napoleon Dynamite’, the hero of the film that bears his name, is a loser. Played by Jon Heder, he lives in the small rural town of Preston, Idaho, which, unsurprisingly, was the home town of the film's co-writer and director, Jared Hess.<br/><br/>Boys regularly bash Napoleon and girl’s flee from him. Napoleon lives with his Gran and his older brother, Kip, (Aaron Ruell), another nerd who spends his time in an internet chat-room; and when Gran is hurt in a dune buggy accident, Uncle Rico, (Jon Gries), comes to stay. <br/><br/>This is a slacker comedy to end all slacker comedies. There's really no coherent plot, but lots of off-the-wall humour as Napoleon tries to get a date, or attempts to help his friend, Pedro, Efren Ramirez, run for school president in opposition to beautiful Summer, (Haylie Duff).<br/><br/>There are quite a few surprises in this engagingly chaotic film, which will probably become a cult success – and don't whatever you do miss the hilarious epilogue, which has been added on after the end credits have completely finished.</p>
<h3>Further comments</h3>
<p>David: Margaret?<br/><br/>Margaret: David, I just sat watching this film with my jaw dropping!<br/><br/>David: (Laughs) I did too. <br/><br/>Margaret: You know what I thought - "Who is this geek?" But, you know, he's got something about him. He's got this beautiful contempt for the world.<br/><br/>David: He's got attitude. <br/><br/>Margaret: Yes, you know? He's not a loser who's just cowed by everybody around him. You know, he's got something in him that's really strong and actually quite attractive.<br/><br/>David: And he comes good at the end. <br/><br/>Margaret: (Laughs) I know.<br/><br/>David: In a way.<br/><br/>Margaret: But do you know what, I also think that this is a film that resonates with the nerd in a lot of men. Because I walked out of the screening and another male critic said to me that that was the nerd that he was at school, except he couldn't dance so well. And I sort of think that other men click into this.<br/><br/>David: Oh, look, I can recognise this too from my school days. I don't say I was like Napoleon, but I wasn't that far off, probably.<br/><br/>Margaret: (Laughs) Could you dance? <br/><br/>David: I couldn't dance either, no.<br/><br/>Margaret: But it's lovely because you think about it afterwards and I think it's one of those comedies that just, with familiarity, just gets funnier and funnier. I'm giving this 3.5 stars. <br/><br/>David: I'm giving it 4. <br/></p>

<i><strong>Score:</strong></i> <img src="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133904im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/four.gif"/><br/><br/>
<i><strong>Remarks:</strong></i> Fortunately for those who have only been represented as a head in a toilet bowl or a face about to be hit by a jock’s fist, geeks emerge from the shadows of the school dance in Napoleon Dynamite, a new movie where even the cool kids are uncool. The film’s eponymous drip resides in a small town in America in which fashion and sensibilities have remained in 1982, even though Napoleon’s brother Kip’s addiction to chat rooms reveals it is set in the present. Although the lead actor, Jon Heder, appears to be trying too hard to be too unhip at times, mostly the comedy works in a broad, South Park way. Make sure you stay seated until the very end or you will miss Kip’s marriage and his serenade to his wife which consists of such touching sentiments as “I love tech</p>
</div>

<i><strong>Remarks:</strong></i> I have only owned 1 DVD in the last 5 years. I've rented over 100 movies in that time. The only movie I every cared to buy was "Monty Python's Holy Grail." 1/2 way into watching this movie with my wife I paused it, logged on to Amazon and bought a copy.<br/>I haven't decided if I liked it better than "Holy Grail" but is is on par. A solid 5/5 stars. I can only give that rating to those two movies, though I give a 4.5 to many.<br/><br/>I grew up in small town Iowa, United States. This was so right on it was hilarious. The way the producers made this movie a montage of the 70's (clothing style, language), 80's (Music - Alphaville, WHen In Rome), and 90s ("World Wide Web") made it even more endearing to a larger audience</p>

$(document).ready(function(){

	// mobile menu
	$("#btnMobileMenu").click(function() {
		$("#mobileMenu").slideToggle('fast');
		return false;
	});		
	
	// autocomplete 
	$("#finda").focus(function() {
		$("body").scrollTo('#finda',1000);
		return false;
	});		
	

	$('#finda').autocomplete({
		lookup: movies,
		lookupLimit: 10,
		minChars:1,
		triggerSelectOnValidInput: false,
		onSelect: function (suggestion) {
			window.location = '/atthemovies/txt/'+suggestion.data+'.htm';
		}
	});	
	
	
	// mobile review pages 
	// movie details 
	if ($(".moviedetails").length) {
		var movieDetailsContent = $(".moviedetails").html();
		$("#movieDetails").html('<h3>Movie Details</h3>'+movieDetailsContent);
	}
	

	
	
	
// end ready
});
